##### 例54：英语—2010年Text 3

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6d9d234d-0f66-4809-a599-230a22f93d92/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_151_1376_225_1434.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A42Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff85b8f8626ebaff9226971488ece2d691bdb8f174f3caf20461898cfff4cab3a" alt="Image" width="6%" />

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6d9d234d-0f66-4809-a599-230a22f93d92/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_151_1376_225_1434.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A42Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff85b8f8626ebaff9226971488ece2d691bdb8f174f3caf20461898cfff4cab3a" alt="Image" width="6%" />

段4 $ ^{①} $

</div>


</div>


① The researchers' argument stems from a simple observation about social influence: With the exception of a few celebrities like Oprah Winfrey—whose outsize presence is primarily a function of media, not interpersonal influence—even the most influential members of a population

simply don't interact with that many others. ②Yet it is precisely these non-celebrity influentials who, according to the two-step-flow theory, are supposed to drive social epidemics, by influencing their friends and colleagues directly. ③For a social epidemic to occur, however, each person so affected must then influence his or her own acquaintances, who must in turn influence theirs, and so on; and just how many others pay attention to each of  $ \underline{\text{these people}} $ has little to do with the initial influential. ④If people in the network just two degrees removed from the initial influential prove resistant, for example, the cascade of change won't propagate very far or affect many people.

34. The underlined phrase "these people" in Paragraph 4 refers to the ones who

[A] stay outside the network of social influence.

[B] have little contact with the source of influence.

[C] are influenced and then influence others.

[D] are influenced by the initial influential.

#### 精讲

语义题考查的是文章中的单词、词组或者句子的含义。很多同学会误以为这类题仅仅是在考查生词，但其实不一定，有时考查的是生词的词义，有时考查的是熟词僻义（熟悉的单词，但是生僻的词义），还有时考查的是单词的指代。常见的提问形式如下：

The word/phrase/expression/sentence “…” (Line..., Paragraph...) most probably means/refers to/denotes/stands for/suggests ___.

· The word "..." (Line..., Paragraph...) is closest in meaning to ___

- What does the author mean by “…” (Line..., Paragraph...)?

By “…” (Line..., Paragraph...), the author means/implies ___

语义题的解题关键就是“根据上下文”推测意思，可以根据上下文中的以下几个方面来推测（尤其前三点最常用）。

1 同义词 / 近义词

2 逻辑对应 / 逻辑相同 / 逻辑相反

3 举例

4 同位语 / 插入语 / 从句

5 标点冒号 / 破折号 / 分号

##### 例45：英语二2018年Text2

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d42e40be-d26b-4549-bd6d-e4399f0d552d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_71_1451_135_1470.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A39Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdb02015cbe0f80518878f309db61318aa75795efc103df58561d9a2bce9ce4ea" alt="Image" width="5%" />

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d42e40be-d26b-4549-bd6d-e4399f0d552d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_71_1451_135_1470.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A39Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdb02015cbe0f80518878f309db61318aa75795efc103df58561d9a2bce9ce4ea" alt="Image" width="5%" />

～

</div>


</div>


段2 ①Some growth stems from a commitment by governments and farsighted businesses to fund cleaner

①部分增长源自政府和有远见的企

业对资助更清洁的能源的承诺。②但越来

energy sources. ②But increasingly the story is about the  $ \underline{\text{plummeting}} $ prices of renewables, especially wind and solar. ③The cost of solar panels has dropped by 80 percent and the cost of wind turbines by close to one-third in the past eight years.

越多的说法是，（这源于）可再生能源价格的暴跌，尤其是风能和太阳能。③在过去8年中，太阳能电池板的价格下降了80%，风力涡轮机的价格也降低了近三分之一。

26 The word  $ \underline{\text{plummeting}} $ (Para. 2) is closest in meaning to _____.

单词 "plummeting" (第二段) 在意思上最接近于_____。

题干定位 根据题干中的 "plummeting" (Para. 2) 可以定位到段 2。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>rising上升</td><td rowspan="4">【段2】②But increasingly the story is about the plummeting prices of renewables, especially wind and solar. ③The cost of solar panels has  $ \underline{\text{dropped}} $ by 80 percent and the cost of wind turbines by close to one-third in the past eight years.本题考查 plummeting 的语义，首先据此定位到段2句②。句②中，plummeting 修饰的是 prices of renewables, especially wind and solar（可再生能源价格，尤其是风能和太阳能）。然后根据上下文确定 plummeting 的语义，句③提到，“太阳能电池板的价格下降了80%”，“风力涡轮机的价格下降了近三分之一”，其中“太阳能电池板”和“风力涡轮机”正好对应句②中的“太阳能”和“风能”，由此可知，句③是句②的具体例证，句②中的 plummeting 和句③的谓语动词 dropped（下降）相对应，含义应一致，即 plummeting 含有“下降”的意思，B选项 falling（下降）符合这一含义，因此 B选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{falling}} $下降</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>changing变化</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>stabilizing稳定</td></tr></table>

根据下文中与 plummeting 对应的同义词 dropped，可以推测出 plummeting 的词义。

##### 例46：2009年Text1

④But don't bother trying to kill off old habits; once those  $ \underline{\text{ruts}} $ of procedure are worn into the brain, they're there to stay. ②Instead, the new habits we deliberately press into ourselves create parallel pathways that can bypass those old roads.

①但是不要自寻烦恼去戒除旧习惯；一旦那些习惯的“辙痕”被印在脑海里，便会根深蒂固。②相反，我们刻意培养的新习惯会创造出相应的（神经）通路，它们能绕过那些旧通路。

### 23 The word  $ \underline{\text{ruts}} $ (Para. 4) is closest in meaning to 单词 "ruts" (第四段) 在含义上最接近

题干定位

根据题干给出的段落信息和关键词 ruts 可以直接定位到段 4。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{tracks}} $.路径，踪迹，车辙。</td><td rowspan="2">【段4】①But don&#x27;t bother trying to kill off old habits; once those ruts of procedure are worn into the brain, they&#x27;re there to stay. ②Instead, the new habits we deliberately press into ourselves create parallel  $ \underline{\text{pathways}} $ that can bypass those old  $ \underline{\text{roads}} $.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>series.系列。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>characteristics.特点，特征。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>段4句①说“一旦那些习惯的ruts被印在脑海里，便会根深蒂固”。句②说“我们刻意培养的新习惯会创造出相应的（神经）通路，它们能绕过那些旧通路”。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>connections.联系。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>上下文中，旧习惯和新习惯对应，ruts 和 pathways、roads 对应，由此可以判断ruts 的含义应该与“路径”相近，所以选择 tracks “路径，踪迹；车辙”，因此A选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">句①中的旧习惯与句②中的新习惯对应，ruts 与下文中的 pathways、roads 对应，由此可以推测出 ruts 的词义。</td></tr></table>

##### 例47：2005年Text4

①Russians have a deep love for their own language and carry large chunks of memorized poetry in their heads, while Italian politicians tend to elaborate speech that would seem old-fashioned to most English-speakers. ②Mr. McWhorter acknowledges that formal language is not strictly necessary, and proposes no radical education reforms—he is really grieving over the loss of something beautiful more than useful. ③We now take our English "on  $ \underline{\text{paper plates}} $ instead of  $ \underline{\text{china}} $. ④A shame, perhaps, but probably an inevitable one.

①俄罗斯人深爱着他们自己的语言，并在脑海中记下了大量的诗歌，而意大利的政治家则倾向于精心准备演讲，这对于大多数讲英语的人来说似乎是过时的。 ②麦克沃特先生承认正式的语言并非完全必不可少的，他也并不建议（进行）彻底的教育改革——他真的只是哀叹那些美丽多过实用的事物的消逝。 ③我们现在“用纸盘子而非瓷盘子”装着我们的英语大餐。 ④这或许令人惋惜，但可能是不可避免的一个（趋势）。

### 40 According to  $ \underline{\text{the last paragraph}} $, "paper plates" is to "china" as 根据最后一段, "纸盘子"之于"瓷盘子"相当于

根据题干的 the last paragraph/paper plates/china，可以定位到最后一段。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>“temporary” is to “permanent”. “临时的”之于“永久的”。</td><td rowspan="2">【段5】②Mr. McWhorter acknowledges that formal language is not strictly necessary, and proposes no radical education reforms—he is really grieving over  $ \underline{\text{the loss of something}} $  $ \underline{\text{beautiful more than useful}} $. ③We now take our English "on paper plates instead of china"."句③指出“我们现在‘用纸盘子而非瓷盘子’装着我们的英语大餐”，上文句②说“麦克沃特哀叹那些美丽多过实用（something beautiful</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>“radical” is to “conservative”. “激进的”之于“保守的”。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \uwave{\text{functional}} $ is to  $ \uwave{\text{artistic}} $。“实用的”之于“艺术的”。</td><td rowspan="2">more than useful) 的事物的消逝”。结合上下文可以推断出，“纸盘子”指的是“实用（useful）但缺乏美感的事物”。类比口语化的非正式英语；“瓷盘子”则对应的是“具有美感（beautiful）的事物”。类比正式英语。根据useful 和 beautiful 可以判断，“纸盘子”与“瓷盘子”之间的关系对应。C选项的functional（实用的）和artistic（艺术的），因此C选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \uwave{\text{humble}} $ is to "noble"。“卑微的”之于“高尚的”。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">paper plates instead of china 与上文的 something beautiful more than useful 相对应，然后根据 beautiful 和 useful 进行同义改写就可以找到正确答案。</td></tr></table>





##### 例48：2003年Text3

①Railroads justify rate discrimination against captive shippers on the grounds that in the long run it reduces everyone's cost. ②If railroads charged all customers the same average rate, they argue, shippers who have the option of switching to trucks or other forms of transportation would do so, leaving remaining customers to shoulder the cost of keeping up the line. ③It's a theory to which many economists subscribe, but in practice it often leaves railroads in the position of determining which companies will flourish and which will fail. ④"Do we really want railroads to be the  $ \underline{\text{arbiters}} $ of who wins and who loses in the marketplace?" asks Martin Bercovici, a Washington lawyer who frequently represents shippers.

①铁路公司证明针对受制的托运商的费率差别对待是合理的，给出的理由是从长远来看，它（这样做）降低了所有人的成本。②他们认为，如果铁路公司收取所有客户相同的平均费率，那么可以选择改用公路运输或其他运输方式的托运商就会这样做，使剩下的客户（托运商）承担维持铁路运营的成本。③这是许多经济学家都赞同的理论，但在实践中它（该理论）常常使得铁路公司处于决定哪家公司盈利和哪家公司亏损的地位。④“难道我们真的想让铁路公司成为决定市场上谁赢谁输的仲裁者吗？”一位经常代表托运商的华盛顿律师马丁·贝科维奇问道。

### The word "  $ \underline{\text{arbiters}} $ " (Para. 4) most probably refers to those 单词 "arbiters" (第四段) 最有可能指的是那些

##### 题干定位 根据题干中的信息可以直接定位到段4句④。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>who work as coordinators. 起协调者作用的人。</td><td rowspan="2">【段4】③...but in practice it often leaves railroads  $ \underline{\text{in the position of determining}} $ which companies will flourish and which will fail. ④"Do we really want railroads to be the arbiters of who wins and who loses in the marketplace?"本题考查 arbiters 的意思，先来看上下文的内容：③……但在实践中它（该理论）常常使得铁路公司处于决定哪家公司盈利和哪家公司亏损的地位。④"难道我们真的想让铁路公司成为决定市场上谁赢谁输的 arbiters 吗？"</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{who function as judges}} $. 起仲裁者作用的人。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>who supervise transactions, 监督交易的人。</td><td rowspan="2">观察上下文，句⑤的leaves railroads对应句④的want railroads，郡表达了“便得/想让铁路公司……”；句③的which companies will flourish and which will fail对应句④的who wins and who loses；因此arbiters则对应in the position of determining，即arbiters“应具有决定的作用，并且能够决定谁赢谁输”，因此B选项正确。其他三个选项均不符合题意，故均错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>who determine the price, 决定价格的人。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">· it often leaves railroads in the position of determining  $ \underline{\text{which companies will flourish}} $ and  $ \underline{\text{which will fall}} $ · Do we really want railroads to be the arbiters of  $ \underline{\text{who wins}} $ and  $ \underline{\text{who loses}} $ 句③和句④的结构对应，如上，根据对应可以推测出arbiters的词义应该与determining 相关，但是并不是D选项，因为这里决定的不是price（价格），因此就找到了determine的同义改写B选项。</td></tr></table>





##### 例49：英语二2013年Text2

①A century ago, the immigrants from across the Atlantic included settlers and sojourners. ②Along with the many folks looking to make a permanent home in the United States came those who had no intention to stay, and who would make some money and then go home. ③Between 1908 and 1915, about 7 million people arrived while about 2 million departed. ④About a quarter of all Italian immigrants, for example, eventually returned to Italy for good. ⑤They even had an affectionate nickname, "uccelli di passaggio,"  $ \underline{\text{birds of passage}} $.

①一个世纪前，横跨大西洋来到美国的移民包括定居者和旅居者。②除了许多希望在美国永久安家的人，还有一些人，他们不打算留下来，想赚点钱然后回家。③1908年到1915年间，大约有700万人抵达（美国），而大约200万人离开了。④例如，大约四分之一的意大利移民最终永久返回了意大利。⑤他们甚至还有一个亲切的昵称——“uccelli di passaggio（候鸟）”。

 $ \underline{\text{“Birds of passage”}} $ refers to those who ___.

“候鸟”指的是那些___的人。

题干定位 根据题干中引号内的信息，可以直接定位到段1句⑤。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{stay in a foreign country}} $  $ \underline{\text{temporarily}} $ 暂时留在国外</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>leave their home countries  $ \underline{\text{for good}} $ 永远离开他们的家乡</td></tr></table>

【段1】①A century ago, the immigrants from  $ \underline{\text{across the Atlantic}} $ included settlers and sojourners. ②Along with the many folks looking to make a  $ \underline{\text{permanent}} $ home in the United States came those who had no intention to stay, and who would make some money and then go home. ④About a quarter of all  $ \underline{\text{Italian immigrants}} $, for example, eventually  $ \underline{\text{returned to Italy for good}} $. ⑤ $ \underline{\text{They}} $ even had an affectionate nickname, "uccelli di passaggio," birds of passage.



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>immigrate across the Atlantic 横跨大西洋移居</td><td rowspan="2">题干考查的内容 Birds of passage 位于段 1 最后一句，该句指出 birds of passage 是对 They 的昵称，They 指代的必然是上一句提到的内容。句④指出，大约四分之一的意大利移民最终永久返回了意大利，由此可知，They 指代的是“永久返回意大利的那些人”，也就是说 Birds of passage 指的就是“永久返回意大利的那些人”。“永久返回意大利”意味着他们只是短暂地留在美国，A 选项 stay in a foreign country temporarily（暂时留在国外）与原文相符，是对 returned to Italy for good（永久返回了意大利）的同义改写，因此 A 选项正确。 余下三个错误选项的详解如下： B 选项 leave their home countries for good（永远离开他们的家乡）与原文内容相反，属于反向干扰，因此 B 选项错误。 C 选项中的 across the Atlantic 在段 1 句①中可以找到，但是横跨大西洋移居的人包括定居者和旅居者，而此处 Birds of passage 仅指后者，因此 C 选项错误。 D 选项中的 permanent 在段 1 句②中可以找到，但文中说的是“在美国永久安家”，与 Birds of passage 所指含义相反，因此 D 选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>find permanent jobs overseas 在海外寻找长期工作</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">句⑤中的 birds of passage 对应句首的 They，而代词 They 指代的是上文句④的内容，据此可以推测出词组的意思。但是这道题的难点其实在于对于上文的理解，句①说移民分为两种人，而句②这个经典的长难句正好是解释上文说的两种移民，理解好了这个长难句，那么整段话的内容，包括这道题，就都迎刃而解。 想多练习考研英语重点的长难句分析，可以跟住静姐学习每日一句长难句，关注静姐的微信公众号“田静老师”或者在其他自媒体平台搜索“考研英语田静”，全年无休免费给大家推送学习内容。</td></tr></table>

##### 例50：英语一2013年Text2

①In December 2010 America's Federal Trade Commission (FTC) proposed adding a "do not track" (DNT) option to internet browsers, so that users could tell advertisers that they did not want to be followed. ②Microsoft's Internet Explorer and Apple's Safari both offer DNT; Google's Chrome is due to do so this year. ③In February the FTC and the Digital Advertising Alliance (DAA) agreed that  $ \underline{\text{the industry}} $ would get cracking on responding to DNT requests.

①2010年12月，美国联邦贸易委员会（FTC）提议在网络浏览器上增加“禁止追踪（DNT）”选项，以便用户能告诉广告商他们不想被追踪。②微软的IE浏览器和苹果的Safari浏览器都提供“禁止追踪”选项；谷歌的Chrome浏览器预计今年也会这么做。③2月，美国联邦贸易委员会（FTC）和数字广告联盟（DAA）达成共识，该行业将立即开始响应“禁止追踪”请求。

 $ \underline{\text{“The industry”(Para. 3)}} $ refers to "The industry" (第三段) 指的是



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>online advertisers.在线广告商。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段3】①In December 2010 America's Federal Trade Commission (FTC) proposed adding a “do not track” (DNT) option to internet browsers, so that users could tell advertisers that they did not want to be followed. ②Microsoft’s Internet Explorer and Apple’s Safari both offer DNT; Google’s Chrome is due to do so this year. ③In February the FTC and the Digital Advertising Alliance (DAA) agreed that the industry would get cracking on responding to DNT requests.段3句③提到...the industry would get cracking on responding to DNT requests（该行业将立即开始响应“禁止追踪”请求），the industry（该行业）指上文提到过的行业，因此要联系上文。句①介绍FTC提议在“网络浏览器”上增加DNT选项；句②提到微软IE、苹果Safari、谷歌Chrome浏览器都提供DNT选项。微软、苹果、谷歌都是浏览器开发商，由此可知本段主要是讲浏览器开发商对DNT的回应，the industry指网络浏览器开发商。因此D选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>e-commerce conductors.电子商务运营商。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>其他三个选项均与原文内容不符，可利用静姐的“灵魂三问”法分析排除：【段3】①In December 2010 America's Federal Trade Commission (FTC) proposed adding a “do not track” (DNT) option to internet browsers, so that users could tell advertisers that they did not want to be followed.根据静姐的“灵魂三问”比对选项和原文：1 有否？有！A选项中的advertisers（广告商）在原文中可以找到。2 全否？不全！原文说“增加‘禁止追踪 (DNT)’选项，以便用户能告诉广告商他们不想被追踪”，这里只提到“广告商”，无法由此得出他们是否都是“在线广告商”，A选项推断过度，因此错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>digital information analysts.数字信息分析者。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>根据静姐的“灵魂三问”法分析：1 有否？有！A选项中的advertisers（广告商）在原文中可以找到。2 全否？不全！原文说“增加‘禁止追踪 (DNT)’选项，以便用户能告诉广告商他们不想被追踪”，这里只提到“广告商”，无法由此得出他们是否都是“在线广告商”，A选项推断过度，因此错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>internet browser developers.网络浏览器开发商。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>根据静姐的“灵魂三问”法分析：1 有否？没有！B选项e-commerce conductors（电子商务运营商）在原文中并未提及，属于无中生有，因此B选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>1 有否？有！ C 选项中的 digital（数字的）在原文中可以找到。2 全否？不全！原文说的是 Digital Advertising Alliance（数字广告联盟）这一机构，并没有提到 digital information analysts（数字信息分析者），属于捏造信息，因此 C 选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">语义题并不一定是考查较难的生词，还有可能考查熟词僻义或上下文的指代，比如本题，大家一定都认识这个词组 The industry，但这里考查的并非它的意思，而是它在这里的上下文中指代什么。根据上文的举例 Microsoft's Internet Explorer、Apple's Safari 和 Google's Chrome，可以推测出 The industry 指代的含义。</td></tr></table>





##### 例51：2002年Text2

①As a result, the modern world is increasingly populated by intelligent  $ \underline{\text{gizmos}} $ whose presence we barely notice but whose universal existence has removed much human labor. ②Our factories hum to the rhythm of robot assembly arms. ③Our banking is done at automated teller terminals that thank us with mechanical politeness for the transaction. ④Our subway trains are controlled by tireless robot-drivers. ⑤And thanks to the continual miniaturization of electronics and micro-mechanics, there are already robot systems that can perform some kinds of brain and bone surgery with submillimeter accuracy—far greater precision than highly skilled physicians can achieve with their hands alone.

①结果，现代世界充斥着越来越多的智能装置，（尽管）我们几乎没有注意到它们的存在，但它们的普遍存在已经解放了大量人类劳动力。②我们的工厂里嗡嗡地响着机器人装配臂的节奏声。③我们的银行业务是在自动柜员终端上完成的，它们还会用机械的礼貌用语感谢我们来交易。④我们的地铁由不知疲倦的机器人司机驾驶。⑤多亏了电子器件和微机械的不断微型化，现在已经有机器人系统能够进行一些精确度达到亚毫米的脑部和骨科的手术，远超技术高超的医生仅凭其双手所能达到的精确度。

### 47 The word  $ \underline{\text{gizmos}} $ (Para. 2) most probably means 单词 "gizmos" (第二段) 最有可能的意思是

题干定位 根据题干中的 "gizmos" (Para. 2) 可以明确定位到段 2。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>programs.程序。</td><td rowspan="2">【段2】①As a result, the modern world is increasingly populated by intelligent gizmos  $ \underline{\text{whose presence we barely notice but whose universal existence has removed much human labor}} $. ②Our factories hum to the rhythm of  $ \underline{\text{robot assembly arms}} $. ③Our banking is done at  $ \underline{\text{automated teller terminals}} $ that thank us with mechanical politeness for the transaction. ④Our subway trains are controlled by tireless  $ \underline{\text{robot-drivers}} $.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>experts.专家。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{devices}} $.设备。</td><td rowspan="2">句①提到 gizmos 的特点是“我们几乎没有注意到它们的存在，但它们的普遍存在已经解放了大量人类劳动力”，据此可排除 B 选项和 D 选项，因为这两者不符合如上 gizmos 的特点。再根据句②-④中用来举例说明 gizmos 的 robot assembly arms（机器人装配臂）、automated feller terminals（自动柜员终端）和 robot-drivers（机器人司机），它们共同的特点是都属于 devices（设备），因此 C 选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>creatures.生物。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">根据 gizmos 后面的定语从句和其后的举例 robot assembly arms（机器人装配臂）、automated feller terminals（自动柜员终端）和 robot-drivers（机器人司机）可以推测出 gizmos 的词义。</td></tr></table>





##### 例52：2004年Text3

①When it comes to the slowing economy,  $ \underline{\text{Ellen Spero isn't biting her nails just yet.}} $ ②But the 47-year-old manicurist isn't cutting, filing or polishing as many nails as she'd like to, either. ③Most of her clients spend 12 to 50 weekly, but last month two longtime customers suddenly stopped showing up. ④Spero blames the softening economy. ⑤"I'm a good economic indicator," she says. ⑥"I provide a service that people can do without when they're concerned about saving some dollars." ⑦So Spero is downscaling, shopping at middle-brow Dillard's department store near her suburban Cleveland home, instead of Neiman Marcus. ⑧"I don't know if other clients are going to abandon me, too," she says.

①谈到经济发展速度放缓时，爱伦·斯佩罗还不至于束手无策。②但是这位47岁的美甲师现在修剪、镂磨、上油的指甲也没有她想要（做）的那样多了。③她的大多数客户每周消费12至50美元，但上个月两位老顾客突然不再出现。④斯佩罗（把这个）归咎于疲软的经济。⑤“我是一个不错的经济指标。”她说。⑥“我提供的是一种当人们想省钱时不要也能行的服务。”⑦因此斯佩罗正在降低（消费）档次，去克利夫兰郊区家附近的迪拉德中档百货商店购物，而不是去内曼·马库斯（高端百货商店）。⑧“我不知道其他顾客是否也会弃我而去。”她说。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="3">51 通过“Ellen Spero isn't biting her nails just yet”(Para.1), the author means通过“Ellen Spero isn't biting her nails just yet”(第一段)，作者表达的意思是题干定位 根据题干给出的明确信息定位到段1。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Spero can hardly maintain her business.斯佩罗几乎无法维持自己的生意。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段1】① When it comes to the slowing economy, Ellen Spero isn't biting her nails just yet. ②  $ \underline{\text{But}} $ the 47-year-old manicurist isn't cutting, filing or polishing as many nails as she'd like to, either. ③ Most of her clients spend 12 to 50 weekly, but last month two longtime customers suddenly stopped showing up. ④ Spero blames the softening economy.想判断句子的语义，解题的关键在于上下文。上文提到，当谈到经济发展速度放缓时，Ellen Spero isn't biting her nails just yet。下</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Spero is too much engaged in her work.斯佩罗过分投入自己的工作。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>文指出，但是她的客人少了，老客户突然不再出现。下文句首的 But 表示转折，转折之后的内容通常与转折之前的内容在语义上是相反的，因此根据 But 之后说的 “对美甲师有负面影响”，可知 But 之前所说的与 But 之后的负面影响相反，即 “对美甲师的影响其实没那么严重”，因此 D 选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Spero has grown out of her bad habit.斯佩罗改掉了她的坏习惯。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>A 选项 “斯佩罗几乎无法维持自己的生意”，与 But 转折之后的内容 “对美甲师有负面影响”，都是负面、否定的内容，即相同方向的内容，不符合上下文之间的转折逻辑，因此 A 选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Spero is not in a desperate situation.斯佩罗还没陷入绝境。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>B 选项无中生有，原文说的是 “美甲师的生意少了”，而不是 “投入工作的程度”，因此 B 选项错误。C 选项其实是用句子的字面意思作为混淆，biting her nails（咬指甲）的确是坏习惯，但是在文中并不是字面的意思，因此 C 选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">根据下文的转折词 But，可以判断出上下文的逻辑相反，据此就可以推断出句子意思的方向。</td></tr></table>





##### 例53: 2006年Text1

①In spite of "endless talk of difference," American society is an amazing machine for  $ \underline{\text{homogenizing}} $ people.

②There is "the democratizing uniformity of dress and discourse, and the casualness and absence of deference" characteristic of popular culture. ③People are absorbed into "a culture of consumption" launched by the 19th-century department stores that offered "vast arrays of goods in an elegant atmosphere. ④Instead of intimate shops catering to a knowledgeable elite" these were stores "anyone could enter, regardless of class or background. ⑤This turned shopping into a public and democratic act."

⑥The mass media, advertising and sports are other forces for homogenization.

①尽管“无休止地谈论差别”，但美国社会是一台使人们同化的惊人机器。

②大众文化具有“着装和言谈的民主化统一，随意和不拘礼节”的特点。③人们被19世纪百货商店推出的“消费文化”同化，这些百货商店“在优雅的氛围中提供种类繁多的商品。④这些不是迎合知识精英的私密商店”，而是“不论阶层和背景，任何人都可以进入的商店。⑤这使得购物成为一种公共的、民主的行为。”⑥大众传媒、广告和体育（也）是同化的其他推动力。

### 21 The word  $ \underline{\text{homogenizing}} $ (Para. 1) most probably means 单词 "homogenizing" (第一段) 最有可能的意思是



<table border="1" style="margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;"><tr><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">[A]</td><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">identifying. 辨别，确认。</td><td rowspan="2">【段1】①In spite of “endless talk of difference,” American society is an amazing machine for homogenizing people. In spite of...表示“尽管……”，在句子中会构成让步转折的关系，即前半句和后半句之间的逻辑关系是让步转折。句①表达的是“尽管‘无休止地谈论差别’，但是美国社会实际上是一台homogenizing</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">[B]</td><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">associating. 联合，联系。</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">[C]</td><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">assimilating. 简化；吸收。</td><td rowspan="2">人们的惊人机器”。转折“但是”前后的内容意思相反，即 homogenizing 与 difference（不同，差异）的意思相反，所以 homogenizing 的意思应该跟“相同”有关，因此 C 选项 assimilating（同化）正确。</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">[D]</td><td style="text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;">monopolizing. 垄断，独占。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">in spite of... 表示“尽管……”，在句子中构成“明让步、暗转折”的关系，即句①的前半句和后半句之间的逻辑关系是让步转折，有转折就意味着逻辑相反，据此可以推测出 homogenizing 的词义。</td></tr></table>




##### 例54：英语一2010年Text3

①The researchers' argument stems from a simple observation about social influence: With the exception of a few celebrities like Oprah Winfrey—whose outsize presence is primarily a function of media, not interpersonal influence—even the most influential members of a population simply don't interact with that many others. ②Yet it is precisely these non-celebrity influentials who, according to the two-step-flow theory, are supposed to drive social epidemics, by influencing their friends and colleagues directly. ③For a social epidemic to occur, however, each person so affected must then influence his or her own acquaintances, who must in turn influence theirs, and so on; and just how many others pay attention to each of  $ \underline{\text{these people}} $ has little to do with the initial influential. ④If people in the network just two degrees removed from the initial influential prove resistant, for example, the cascade of change won't propagate very far or affect many people.

①研究人员的论据源于对社会影响的一项简单观察：除了像奥普拉·温弗瑞这样的少数名人——超级影响力主要是由媒体而不是人际关系带来的——即使是群体中最有影响力的成员也不会与那么多人互动。②而根据两级流动理论，恰恰是这些不是名人但具有影响力的人，通过直接影响他们的朋友和同事，从而推动了社会潮流的发展。③然而，要形成一种社会流行潮流，每个受影响的人必须接着影响他或她自己的熟人，这些人又必须再影响他们的熟人，如此延续；这些人中的每个人能得到多少人关注与最初有影响力的人并无多大关系。④例如，在这个人际影响网络中，如果那些与最初有影响力的人仅相隔两个层级的人（对这种影响）采取抵制态度，那么这一连串的变化就不会传播得太远，也不会影响很多人。

### 34 The underlined phrase  $ \underline{\text{these people}} $  $ \underline{\text{in Paragraph 4}} $ refers to the ones who 第四段中画线的词组 "these people" 指的是那些

题干定位 根据题干中明确的段落信息和关键词 these people 定位到段 4。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>stay outside  $ \underline{\text{the network}} $ of social  $ \underline{\text{influence}} $.处于社交影响网络之外的人。</td></tr></table>



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段4】③For a social epidemic to occur, however,  $ \underline{\text{each}} $ person so affected must then influence his or her own acquaintances, who must in turn influence theirs, and so on; and just how many others pay attention to each of these</td></tr></table>



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>have little contact with the source of influence.与影响源很少接触的人。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>people has little to do with the initial influential.本题问 these people 的具体指代对象，先来看其所在的上下文。观察段4句③，分号和其后的and标示平行（并列）结构。分号前说“要形成一种社会流行潮流，每个受影响的人必须接着影响他或她自己的熟人，这些人又必须再影响他们的熟人，如此延续”，表明形成社会流行潮流的条件是受影响的人再去影响别人；分号后说“这些人（these people）中的每个人能得到多少人关注与最初有影响力的人并无多大关系”，由此不难推知，these people 指的就是分号前说的“受影响再去影响别人的人”，因此C选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>are influenced and then influence others.受他人影响又影响他人的人。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段4】④If people in the network just two degrees removed from the initial influential prove resistant, for example, the cascade of change won't propagate very far or affect many people.A选项利用段4句④中的the network（网络）、influential（有影响力的）和affect（影响）设置干扰。但原文说的是“如果那些与最初有影响力的人仅相隔两个层级的人”，这里讲述的是人际影响网络中的人，A选项 stay outside the network of social influence（处于社交影响网络之外的人）与原文相悖，反向干扰，因此A选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>are influenced by the initial influential.受最初的有影响力人士影响的人。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段4】③For a social epidemic to occur, however, each B选项利用原文的have little（有很少）和the initial influential（最初有影响力的人）设置干扰。原文说的是“这些人（these people）中的每个人能得到多少人关注与最初有影响力的人（影响源）并无多大关系”，但选项说“与影响源很少接触的人”，与原文不符，属于于曲解原文，因此B选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>人（these people）中的每个人能得到多少人关注与最初有影响力的人并无多大关系”，说明这些人（these people）并非都是被最初的有影响力的人所影响的，而D选项说“受最初的有影响力人士影响的人”，与原文不符，因此D选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">代词通常是指代上文的，这里的these people自然也是；而且句③中these people所在的后半句与前半句之间是and连接，表示前后内容之间是顺接的并列关系，即逻辑相同，据此就可以根据上半句的内容推测出these people指代的含义。</td></tr></table>

段① Death is normal; we are genetically programmed to disintegrate and perish, even under ideal conditions. ② We all understand that at some level, yet as medical consumers we treat death as a problem to be solved. ③ Shielded by third-party payers from the cost of our care, we demand everything that can possibly be done for us, even if it's useless. ④ The most obvious example is late-stage cancer care. ⑤ Physicians—frustrated by their inability to cure the disease and fearing loss of hope in the patient—too often offer aggressive treatment far beyond what is scientifically justified.

57. The author uses the example of cancer patients to show that

[A] medical resources are often wasted.

[B] doctors are helpless against fatal diseases.

[C] some treatments are too aggressive.

[D] medical costs are becoming unaffordable.

##### 例56：英语二2013年Text1

段4 ① Yes, new technology has been eating jobs forever, and always will. ② But there's been an acceleration. ③ As Davidson notes, "In the 10 years ending in 2009, [U.S.] factories shed workers so fast that they erased almost all the gains of the previous 70 years; roughly one out of every three manufacturing jobs—about 6 million in total—disappeared."

① There will always be change—new jobs, new products, new services. ② But the one thing we know for sure is that with each advance in globalization and the I. T. revolution, the best jobs will require workers to have more and better education to make themselves above average.

23. The quotation in Paragraph 4 explains that ___.

[A] gains of technology have been erased

[B] job opportunities are disappearing at a high speed

[C] factories are making much less money than before

[D] new jobs and services have been offered

##### 例57：2009年Text4

① We should not forget, however, that most New Englanders were less well educated.

② While few craftsmen or farmers, let alone dependents and servants, left literary compositions to be analyzed. it is obvious that their views were less fully intellectualized. ③ Their thinking often had a traditional superstitious quality. ④ A tailor named John Dane, who emigrated in the late 1630s, left an account of his reasons for leaving England that is filled with signs. ⑤ Sexual confusion, economic frustrations, and religious hope—all came together in a decisive moment when he opened the Bible, told his father that the first line he saw would settle his fate, and read the magical words: "Come out from among them, touch no unclean thing, and I will be your God and you shall be my people." ⑥ One wonders what Dane thought of the careful sermons explaining the Bible that he heard in puritan churches.

39. The story of John Dane shows that less well-educated New Englanders were often

[A] influenced by superstitions.

[B] troubled with religious beliefs.

[C] puzzled by church sermons.

[D] frustrated with family earnings.

##### 例58：2003年Text2

④ Leaders of the animal rights movement target biomedical research because it depends on public funding, and few people understand the process of health care research. ⑤ Hearing allegations of cruelty to animals in research settings, many are perplexed that anyone would deliberately harm an animal.

① For example, a grandmotherly woman staffing an animal rights booth at a recent street fair was distributing a brochure that encouraged readers not to use anything that comes from or is tested in animals—no meat, no fur, no medicines. ② Asked if she opposed immunizations, she wanted to know if vaccines come from animal research. ③ When assured that they do, she replied, "Then I would have to say yes." ④ Asked what will happen when epidemics return, she said, "Don't worry, scientists will find some way of using computers." ⑤ Such well-meaning people just don't understand.

48. The example of the grandmotherly woman is used to show the public's

[A] discontent with animal research.

[B] ignorance about medical science.

[C] indifference to epidemics.

[D] anxiety about animal rights.

##### 例59：英语一2019年Text1

22. Alfred Marshall is quoted to indicate

[A] the solid structure of publicly traded companies.

[B] governments' impatience in decision-making.

[C] the conditions for generating quick profits.

[D] "short-termism" in economic activities.

① In fact, "becoming more efficient" is part of the problem. ② Thinking of time as a resource to be maximised means you approach it instrumentally, judging any given moment as well spent only in so far as it advances progress toward some goal. ③ Immersive reading, by contrast, depends on being willing to risk inefficiency, goallessness, even time-wasting. ④ Try to slot it in as a to-do list item and you'll manage only goal-focused reading—useful, sometimes, but not the most fulfilling kind. ⑤ "The future comes at us like empty bottles along an unstoppable and nearly infinite conveyor belt," writes Gary Eberle in his book Sacred Time, and "we feel a pressure to fill these different-sized bottles (days, hours, minutes) as they pass, for if they get by without being filled, we will have wasted them." ⑥ No mind-set could be worse for losing yourself in a book.

32. The "empty bottles" metaphor illustrates that people feel a pressure to ___.

[A] update their to-do lists

[B] make passing time fulfilling

[C] carry their plans through

[D] pursue carefree reading

##### 例62：英语二2018年Text3

① The product they're selling is data, and we, the users, convert our lives to data for the benefit of the digital giants. ② Just as some ants farm the bugs called aphids for the honeydew they produce when they feed, so Google farms us for the data that our digital lives yield. ③ Ants keep predatory insects away from where their aphids feed; Gmail keeps the spammers out of our inboxes. ④ It doesn't feel like a human or democratic relationship, even if both sides benefit.

35. The ants analogy is used to illustrate ___.

[A] a typical competition pattern among digital giants

[B] a win-win business model between digital giants

[C] the benefits provided for digital giants' customers

[D] the relationship between digital giants and their users

#### 精讲

· The example of... is used to show ___.

写作目的题考查的是文章中的举例、引用或比喻等被使用是为了表达什么。常见的提问方式有：

· The author uses the example of... to show that _____.

· ...is mentioned in Paragraph XXX to present ___.

· ...is used to illustrate ___.

· The quotation in Paragraph XXX explains that ___.

· ...is quoted to indicate ___.

这类题的解题关键是区分清楚“写作内容”和“写作目的”。“写作内容”指的就是举例、引用或比喻的内容本身，通过题干的关键词就可以在原文中定位找到；而“写作目的”指的是举例、引用或比喻被用

来表达的观点或主旨，位置通常在“写作内容”之前或之后。

我们通常的解题习惯是通过题干在原文中定位，然后在定位的位置找答案。但写作目的题的解题关键就在于“题干定位的地方不是答案”，因为题干定位的是“写作内容”本身，而它所服务的“写作目的”要在定位的前后找。写作目的题的错误选项经常是利用举例、引用或比喻的内容细节来出的。很多同学会觉得既然举例或引用的内容不是正确答案所在，那是不是可以略去看呢？不行！因为最近两年的真题有一个变化的趋势，写作目的题的正确答案必须要结合例子或引用的内容才能理解，所以不看不行。

##### 例55：2003年Text4

①Death is normal; we are genetically programmed to disintegrate and perish, even under ideal conditions.

②We all understand that at some level, yet as medical consumers we treat death as a problem to be solved.

③Shielded by third-party payers from the cost of our care, we demand everything that can possibly be done for us, even if it's useless. ④The most obvious example is late-stage  $ \underline{\text{cancer}} $ care. ⑤Physicians—frustrated by their inability to cure the disease and fearing loss of hope in the patient—too often offer aggressive treatment far beyond what is scientifically justified.

①死亡是正常的；我们的基因决定即使在理想的条件下（我们）也必将会衰老和死亡。②我们所有人在某种程度上都理解这一点，但作为医疗消费者，我们把死亡当作一个需要被解决的问题。③（因为）被第三方付款人保护免交医疗保健费用，（所以）我们要求（用尽）一切可能的医疗手段，即使它们毫无用处。④最明显的例子就是晚期癌症治疗。⑤医生——对无法治愈这种疾病感到沮丧，同时又担心病人失去希望——常常采用极端大胆的、远远超出科学合理性的治疗方法。

### 57 The author uses the example of  $ \underline{\text{cancer}} $ patients to show that作者使用癌症患者的例子是为了表明

根据题干中的关键词 cancer 定位到段 2。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>medical resources are often wasted.医疗资源经常被浪费。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段2】③Shielded by third-party payers from the cost of our care, we demand everything that can possibly be done for us. even if it's useless.④The most obvious example is late-stage cancer care.⑤Physicians—frustrated by their inability to cure the disease and fearing loss of hope in the patient—too often offer aggressive treatment far beyond what is scientifically justified.根据题干中的关键词 cancer 定位到段2，其中句④～⑤是例子细节。“最明显的例子就是晚期癌症治疗。医生——对无法治愈这种疾病感到沮丧，同时又担心病人失去希望——常常采用极端大胆的、远远超出科学合理性的治疗方法。”例子之前的句③是例子所支持的观点，“（因为）被第三方付款人保护免交医疗保健费用，（所以）我们要求（用尽）一切可能的医疗手段，即使它们毫无用处”，也就是说即使是没用的医疗手段也要用，即医疗资源被浪费，A选项是对原文的同义改写，因此A选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{doctors are helpless against fatal diseases}} $.医生对致命的疾病无能为力。</td><td rowspan="2">【段2】④The most obvious example is late-stage cancer care.⑤Physicians—frustrated by their inability to cure the  $ \underline{\text{disease}} $ and fearing loss of hope in the patient—too often offer  $ \underline{\text{aggressive treatment}} $ far beyond what is scientifically justified.B选项doctors are helpless against fatal diseases (医生对致命的疾病无能为力)对应原文Physicians—frustrated by their inability to cure the disease (医生——对无法治愈这种疾病感到沮丧)，属于同义改写。C选项treatments (治疗方法)和aggressive (大胆的)在原文中可以找到。尽管B选项和C选项的内容都能在原文中找到，但是由于它们都是例子的内容细节，而不是例子的写作目的，因此B选项和C选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>some  $ \underline{\text{treatments}} $ are too  $ \underline{\text{aggressive}} $.一些治疗方法过于大胆。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>medical costs are becoming unaffordable.医疗费用正变得负担不起。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>D选项利用下文段3的前三句进行干扰，但那并不是例子说明的观点。因此D选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">先在原文中定位，找到例子位于段2句④～句⑤，而在其之前的句③就是它所服务的写作目的。注意B和C两个选项，虽然它们的内容都能在原文中找到完全的对应，但是它们都是例子的内容本身，而不是例子的写作目的。</td></tr></table>





##### 例56：英语二2013年Text1

①Yes, new technology has been eating jobs forever, and always will. ②But there's been an acceleration. ③As Davidson notes, "In the 10 years ending in 2009, [U.S.] factories shed workers so fast that they erased almost all the gains of the previous 70 years; roughly one out of every three manufacturing jobs—about 6 million in total—disappeared."

①There will always be change—new jobs, new products, new services. ②But the one thing we know for sure is that with each advance in globalization and the I. T. revolution, the best jobs will require workers to have more and better education to make themselves above average.

①是的，新技术一直在蚕食工作（机会），而且将永远持续下去。②但已经出现了加速（的情况）。③正如戴维森所说：“2009年之前的10年里，（美国）工厂裁员的速度如此之快，以至于几乎抵消了过去70年增加的所有（工人的人数）；大约三分之一的制造业岗位——总计约600万个——消失了。”

①变化将永远存在——新工作、新产品、新服务。②但我们可以肯定的一件事是，随着全球化和信息技术革命的每一次进步，最好的工作（岗位）将要求工作者接受更多、更好的教育，以使自己超越平庸。

 $ \underline{\text{The quotation}} $ in  $ \underline{\text{Paragraph 4}} $ explains that ___.

第四段的引用解释了___。

题干定位 根据题干中明确的段落信息和关键词 The quotation 定位到段 4 句③。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>gains of technology have been erased技术成果已被抹去</td><td rowspan="2">【段4】①Yes, new technology has been eating jobs forever, and always will. ②But there&#x27;s been an acceleration. ③As Davidson notes, &quot;In the 10 years ending in 2009, [U.S.] factories shed workers so fast that they erased almost all the gains of the previous 70 years; roughly one out of every three manufacturing jobs—about 6 million in total—disappeared.&quot;段4句③中有引用的具体内容：“2009年之前的10年里，（美国）工厂裁员的速度如此之快……大约三分之一的制造业岗位——总计约600万个——消失了”。观察引用内容前后，段4句①~②指出，新技术一直在蚕食工作机会，而且将永远持续下去，但已经出现了加速的情况。由此可见，此处的引用是用具体数据来说明工作机会消失之快。B选项“就业机会正在快速消失”是对原文的同义改写，且符合本段主旨，因此B选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>job opportunities are disappearing at a high speed就业机会正在快速消失</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>factories are making much less money than before工厂赚的钱比以前少多了</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段4】③As Davidson notes, &quot;In the 10 years ending in 2009, [U.S.] factories shed workers so fast that they erased almost all the gains of the previous 70 years; roughly one out of every three manufacturing jobs—about 6 million in total—disappeared.&quot;A选项利用原文中的个别单词gains和erased设置干扰，但原文中gains指的是过去70年增加的工人人数，并不是技术成果，选项偷换概念，因此A选项错误。段4主要讲述新技术导致就业机会正在快速消失，并未提及工厂的收入问题，C选项所述与段落主旨不符，属于无中生有，因此C选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>new jobs and services have been offered新工作和新服务已经被提供</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段5】①There will always be change—new jobs, new products, new services.D选项中的new jobs and services在段5句①中可以找到，但原文说的是变化将永远存在，即社会一直在变化，并未提到新工作和新服务“已经被提供”，选项捏造信息，且段4中的引用提到了大量工作岗位的消失，D选项与段落主旨不符，因此D选项错误。</td></tr></table>

##### 例57：2009年Text4

①We should not forget, however, that most  $ \underline{\text{New Englanders}} $ were  $ \underline{\text{less well educated}} $. ②While few craftsmen or farmers, let alone dependents and servants, left literary compositions to be analyzed, it is obvious that their views were less fully intellectualized. ③Their thinking often had a traditional superstitious quality. ④A tailor named  $ \underline{\text{John Dane}} $, who emigrated in the late 1630s, left an account of his reasons for leaving England that is filled with signs. ⑤Sexual confusion, economic frustrations, and religious hope—all came together in a decisive moment when he opened the Bible, told his father that the first line he saw would settle his fate, and read the magical words: "Come out from among them, touch no unclean thing, and I will be your God and you shall be my people." ⑥One wonders what Dane thought of the careful sermons explaining the Bible that he heard in puritan churches.

①然而，我们不应该忘记，大多数新英格兰人没有受过良好教育。②尽管极少有工匠或农民（更不用说侍从和仆人了）留下可供分析的文学作品，但显然的是他们的观点并不那么完全理智。③他们的思想往往带有一种传统的迷信色彩。④一位名为约翰·戴恩的裁缝于17世纪30年代末移民了，他留下的关于离开英格兰的理由的叙述中充满了各种神迹。⑤性的困惑、经济挫折和宗教希望——所有这些在关键性的一刻都一起涌现，他打开《圣经》，告诉父亲，他看到的第一行字将决定他的命运，然后他读出以下神奇的话语：“从他们中间走出来，不要沾染不洁之物，我愿成为你的上帝，你将成为我的子民。”⑥人们想知道，戴恩在清教徒教堂里听到精心诠释《圣经》的布道时会做何感想。

### The story of  $ \underline{\text{John Dane}} $ shows that  $ \underline{\text{less well-educated}} $  $ \underline{\text{New Englanders}} $ were often 约翰·戴恩的故事表明受教育程度较低的新英格兰人经常



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>题干定位</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>根据题干关键词 John Dane/less well-educated/New Englanders 定位到段 4。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{influenced by}} $  $ \underline{\text{superstitions}} $. 受到迷信的影响。</td></tr></table>



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>troubled with  $ \underline{\text{religious}} $ beliefs.受到宗教信仰的困扰。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段4】⑤Sexual confusion, economic frustrations, and  $ \underline{\text{religious}} $ hope—all came together in a decisive moment when he opened the Bible...原文说的是religious hope（宗教希望），而非B选项中的“受到宗教信仰的困扰”，因此B选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>puzzled by  $ \underline{\text{church}} $  $ \underline{\text{sermons}} $.对教堂的布道感到困惑。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段4】⑥One wonders what Dane thought of the careful  $ \underline{\text{sermons}} $ explaining the Bible that he heard in puritan  $ \underline{\text{churches}} $.原文指出“人们想知道，戴恩在清教徒教堂里听到精心诠释《圣经》的布道时会做何感想”，并没有提到“对布道感到困惑”，C选项只是利用原文中的churches/sermons设置干扰，因此C选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{frustrated with family earnings}} $.对家庭收入感到失望。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段4】⑤Sexual confusion,  $ \underline{\text{economic frustrations}} $，and religious hope—all came together in a decisive moment when he opened the Bible...选项frustrated with family earnings（对家庭收入感到失望）是对原文中economic frustrations（经济挫折）的同义改写，但这不是所有新英格兰早期移民的特征，这是戴恩的个人经历，因此D选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">这道题的特别之处在于例子和观点之间的分界线泾渭分明。根据题干中的人名 John Dane 去原文中定位，就找到了句④～⑥这部分是举例的内容，因为都有出现这个人。然后在定位处之前的句③中找到了例子服务的观点，则正确答案为A选项。而本题的三个错误选项都是利用了句④～⑥中例子的内容细节来捏造的混淆项，所以区分清楚例子和观点之间的分界线很重要。</td></tr></table>

##### 例58：2003年Text2

④Leaders of the animal rights movement target biomedical research because it depends on public funding, and few people understand the process of health care research. ⑤Hearing allegations of cruelty to animals in research settings, many are perplexed that anyone would deliberately harm an animal.

段2 ①For example,  $ \underline{\text{a grandmotherly woman}} $ staffing an animal rights booth at a recent street fair was distributing a brochure that encouraged readers not to use anything that comes from or is tested in animals—no meat, no fur, no medicines. ②Asked if she opposed immunizations, she wanted to know if vaccines come from animal research. ④动物权利运动的领导人将矛头指向生物医学研究，因为它依赖于公共资金，而且很少有人了解医疗保健研究的过程。 ⑤听到对（医学）研究场所中残忍对待动物的指控时，许多人感到费解，竟然有人会故意伤害动物。

①例如，在最近的街头集市上，一位在动物权利宣传展位工作的老奶奶在分发一本小册子，（小册子）劝告读者不要使用任何动物制品或经过动物实验的东西——包括肉类、毛皮和药物。②被问及她是否反对免疫接种（时），她想知道疫苗是否来自动物实验。③当被告知的确如此（疫苗

③When assured that they do, she replied, "Then I would have to say yes." ④Asked what will happen when epidemics return, she said, "Don't worry, scientists will find some way of using computers." ⑤Such well-meaning people just don't understand.

确实来自动物实验）时，她答道：“那么我不得不说，是的（我反对接种）。” ④被问及流行病再次爆发时会发生什么（时），她说：“别担心，科学家们将会找到利用计算机（解决问题）的方法。” ⑤这些好心的人就是不了解（状况）。

### 48 The example of  $ \underline{\text{the grandmotherly woman}} $ is used to show the public's  老奶奶这个例子被用来说明公众

定位 根据题干中的 the grandmotherly woman 定位到原文段2。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>discontent with animal research.对动物实验的不满。</td><td rowspan="4">【段1】④Leaders of the animal rights movement target biomedical research because it depends on public funding, and few people understand the process of health care research。【段2】①～④例子细节⑤ $ \underline{\text{Such well-meaning people just don&#x27;t understand}} $.段2句①至句④是例子的细节，一位在动物权利宣传展位工作的老奶奶在发宣传册，劝告读者不要使用任何动物制品或经过动物实验的东西。例子之后的句⑤总结“这些好心的人就是不了解（状况）”；例子之前的段1句④指出“很少有人了解医疗保健研究的过程”，根据例子前后的观点可判断出例子的写作目的就是突出“很多人对医疗保健研究的不了解”，即对应B选项ignorance about medical science（对医疗科学的无知），其中ignorance（无知）是对don&#x27;t understand（不了解）的同义改写，因此B选项正确。A选项discontent with animal research（对动物实验的不满）是段1中表达的事实，但不是例子的写作目的，例子是在说明“对动物实验不满的原因是不了解”，因此A选项错误。C选项中的epidemics（流行病）是例子的细节内容，但不是写作的目的，这是典型的混淆项；而且原文中并没有说“老奶奶漠不关心”，只是说“老奶奶认为科学家会解决”，因此C选项错误。D选项利用原文中出现的关键词animal rights（动物权利）进行干扰，但这与例子不相关，因此D选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{ignorance about medical science}} $。对医疗科学的无知。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>indifference to epidemics.对流行病漠不关心。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>anxiety about animal rights.对动物权利的忧虑。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">这道题的选项非常具有迷惑性，但是大家要时刻记得例子的内容细节是“写作内容”，而不是“写作</td></tr></table>

这道题的选项非常具有迷惑性，但是大家要时刻记得例子的内容细节是“写作内容”，而不是“写作目的”。例如段2中句①~④都是例子的内容，所以其中的内容如果出现在选项中则不正确。

##### 例59：英语一2019年Text1

段② ① "Short-termism," or the desire for quick profits, has worsened in publicly traded companies, says the Bank of England's top economist, Andrew Haldane. ② $ \underline{\text{He quotes}} $ a giant of classical economics,  $ \underline{\text{Alfred Marshall}} $, in ① "短期主义" , 或者说是对快速盈利的渴求，在各上市公司中已经加剧，英格兰银行首席经济学家安德鲁·霍尔丹说。②他引用古典经济学伟人阿尔弗雷德·马歇尔的话描述这种金融上的毫无耐

describing this financial impatience as acting like "children who pick the plums out of their pudding to eat them at once" rather than putting them aside to be eaten last,

心——表现得就像“孩子们把李子从他们的布丁里挑出来立刻吃掉”一样，而不是把它们放到一边最后再吃。

###  $ \underline{\text{Alfred Marshall is quoted}} $ to indicate 引用阿尔弗雷德·马歇尔的言论是为了说明



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="3">题干定位 题干中的人名 Alfred Marshall 在原文中可以找到；题干中的 Alfred Marshall is quoted (阿尔弗雷德·马歇尔的话被引用) 对应原文中的 quotes... Alfred Marshall (引用阿尔弗雷德·马歇尔的话)，属于主被动的同义改写，由此可以定位到段2句②。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>the solid structure of publicly traded companies. 上市公司的稳固结构。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段2】① “Short-termism,” or the desire for quick profits, has worsened in publicly traded companies, says the Bank of England’s top economist, Andrew Haldane. ② He quotes a giant of classical economics, Alfred Marshall, in describing this financial impatience as acting like “children who pick the plums out of their pudding to eat them at once” rather than putting them aside to be eaten last. 首先定位原文中引用 Alfred Marshall 的话，即段2句②后半部分中的 “children who pick the plums out of their pudding to eat them at once” rather than putting them aside to be eaten last (“孩子们把李子从他们的布丁里挑出来立刻吃掉”，而不是把它们放到一边最后再吃)。 然后在引用的内容前后找观点，确定答案。句②前半部分提到 “他引用古典经济学伟人阿尔弗雷德·马歇尔的话描述这种金融上的毫无耐心”，可知引用 Alfred Marshall 的话是为了描述 “这种金融上的毫无耐心” (this financial impatience)，而后者又对应句①中的内容，即 “Short-termism,” or the desire for quick profits (“短期主义”，或者说是对快速盈利的渴求)。 D 选项 “Short-termism” in economic activities (经济活动中的 “短期主义”) 符合原文，是对原文句①和句②中观点内容的同义改写，因此 D 选项正确。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>governments’ impatience in decision-making. 政府在决策上没有耐心。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>余下三个错误选项的详解如下：【段2】① “Short-termism,” or the desire for quick profits, has worsened in publicly traded companies, says the Bank of England’s top economist, Andrew Haldane. A 选项中的 publicly traded companies (上市公司) 在原文中可以找到。但原文说 “‘短期主义’，或者说是对快速盈利的渴求，在各上市公司中已经加剧”，并未提到上市公司的结构，也未提到其稳固与否，选项属于捏造信息，因此 A 选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{the}} $ conditions  $ \underline{\text{for}} $ generating  $ \underline{\text{quick profits}} $.产生快速盈利的条件。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段2】②He quotes a giant of classical economics, Alfred Marshall, in describing this financial  $ \underline{\text{impatience}} $ as acting like "children who pick the plums out of their pudding to eat them at once" rather than putting them aside to be eaten last.B 选项中的impatience（不耐心）在原文中可以找到。但原文说的是企业在金融上的急躁表现，而非“政府”或“决策上的”，B 选项“政府在决策上没有耐心”与原文不符，属于捏造信息，因此 B 选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{"short-termism"in economic activities}} $.经济活动中的“短期主义”。</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段2】①“Short-termism,” or  $ \underline{\text{the}} $ desire  $ \underline{\text{for quick profits}} $, has worsened in publicly traded companies, says the Bank of England's top economist, Andrew Haldane.C 选项中的 the... for... quick profits 在原文中可以找到。原文说的是 the desire for quick profits（对快速盈利的渴求），表现的是一种心理愿望，而 C 选项是 the conditions for generating quick profits（产生快速盈利的条件），与原文不符，属于捏造信息，因此 C 选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">先在原文中定位，通过引号可以快速找到引用的内容，然后再往前看，自然就找到了它所服务的写作目的。注意：不仅要看定位到的句②的前半句，还要结合上文的句①一起看。</td></tr></table>





##### 例60：英语二2016年Text3

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f60d8584-6b01-4fc5-91eb-2f8fcb697b91/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_144_900_216_919.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2Fec9bd501268f9842b65e42e53c6b35f3a97031a7f0bd4e11e14e42b446a4faf2" alt="Image" width="6%" />

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f60d8584-6b01-4fc5-91eb-2f8fcb697b91/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_144_900_216_919.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2Fec9bd501268f9842b65e42e53c6b35f3a97031a7f0bd4e11e14e42b446a4faf2" alt="Image" width="6%" />

～

</div>


</div>


①In fact, "becoming more efficient" is part of the problem. ②Thinking of time as a resource to be maximised means you approach it instrumentally, judging any given moment as well spent only in so far as it advances progress toward some goal. ③Immersive reading, by contrast, depends on being willing to risk inefficiency, goallessness, even time-wasting. ④Try to slot it in as a to-do list item and you'll manage only goal-focused reading—useful, sometimes, but not the most fulfilling kind. ⑤"The future comes at us like  $ \underline{\text{empty bottles}} $ along an unstoppable and nearly infinite conveyor belt," writes Gary Eberle in his book Sacred Time, and "we  $ \underline{\text{feel a pressure to}} $ fill these different-sized bottles (days, hours, minutes) as they pass, for if they get by without being filled, we will have wasted them." ⑥No mind-set could be worse for losing yourself in a book.

①事实上，“变得更高效”就是问题的一部分。②把时间看作一种要最大化利用的资源，意味着你（是）功利性地对待时间，认为每一刻都可以充分利用，只要在这一刻朝着某一既定目标迈进。③相比之下，沉浸式阅读取决于（你）愿意冒低效率、无目标甚至浪费时间的风险。④试图像完成任务清单一样给它（阅读）安排时间，你将只能进行目标集中式阅读——有时候有用，但并非最令人满意的那种。⑤“未来就像空瓶子一样沿着不可阻挡且几乎无限的传送带向我们走来，”盖瑞·埃伯利在他的书《神圣的时间》里写道，“当这些不同大小的瓶子（天，小时，分钟）经过时，要填满它们，我们就会感觉到压力，因为如果它们没有被填满就过去的话，我们就是浪费了时间。”⑥对于让你自己沉浸在一本书中来说，没有什么思维模式比这（填满时间的思维方式）更糟糕了。

The  $ \underline{\text{empty bottles}} $ metaphor illustrates that people  $ \underline{\text{feel a pressure to}} $ ____。“空瓶子”的隐喻阐明了人们对_____感到有压力。

题干定位 根据题干中的 empty bottles/feel a pressure to 可以定位到段 3 句⑤。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td rowspan="2">[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>update their to-do lists\n更新他们的任务清单</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>make passing time ful-filling\n让流逝的时间过得有意义</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>carry their plans through完成他们的计划</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>pursue carefree reading\n追求无忧无虑的阅读</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td></tr></table>

本题的题干中部分内容可以逐词与原文对应，通过这种精准定位可以直接找到答案。

##### 例61：英语二2018年Text1

段2 ①Mr. Koziatek is part of something pioneering.

②He is a teacher at a New Hampshire high school where learning is not something of books and tests and mechanical memorization, but practical. ③When did it become accepted wisdom that students should be able to name the 13th president of the United States but be utterly overwhelmed by  $ \underline{\text{a broken bike chain}} $?

①科齐亚特克先生是一次开创之举的参与者。②他是新罕布什尔州一所高中的老师，在那里，学习并不关乎书本、考试和机械记忆，而（在于）实践。③学生们应该能够说出美国第13任总统的名字，却被一根断了的自行车链条弄得完全不知所措，这何时成了一种常理呢？

21  $ \underline{\text{A broken bike chain}} $ is mentioned to show students' lack of _____. (文章)提及一根断了的自行车链条是为了说明学生缺乏_____。

根据题干中的 A broken bike chain（一根断了的自行车链条），定位到段 2。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>practical ability实践能力</td><td rowspan="3">【段2】②He is a teacher at a New Hampshire high school where  $ \underline{\text{learning}} $ is not something of books and tests and  $ \underline{\text{mechanical memorization}} $, but practical. ③When did it become accepted wisdom that students should be able to name the 13th president of the United States but be utterly overwhelmed by a broken bike chain?首先根据题干中的A broken bike chain定位到段2句③的例子，然后在例子的前后找观点，自然可得知上文的句②是其所服务的观点。句②指出，“学习并不关乎书本、考试和机械记忆，而（在于）实践”。而句③中的两个例子正好对应句②的这两个方面，其中“说出美国第13任总统的名字”对应“书本、考试和机械记忆”，而a broken bike chain（一根断了的自行车链条）对应practical（实践的）。A选项practical ability（实践能力）符合文意，因此A选项正确。其他三个错误选项的详解如下：【段2】②He is a teacher at a New Hampshire high school where  $ \underline{\text{learning}} $ is not something of books and tests and  $ \underline{\text{mechanical memorization}} $, but practical.B选项academic training（学术训练）对应原文中的books and tests（书本、考试），D选项mechanical memorization（机械记忆）在原文中可以找到；但原文出现了明确的否定词not，两个选项对应的是表示否定的前半部分，而不是后半部分强调的“实践”，反向干扰，因此B、D选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>academic training学术训练</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>pioneering spirit开创精神</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[D]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>$ \underline{\text{mechanical memorization}} $ 机械记忆</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>【段2】①Mr. Koziatek is part of something  $ \underline{\text{pioneering}} $. C选项中的pioneering（开创性的）在原文中可以找到，但原文说的是“科齐亚特克先生是一次开创之举的参与者”，而题干问的是“一根断了的自行车链条是为了说明学生缺乏什么”，答非所问，因此C选项错误。</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">这道题的特别之处在于其中举出了两个例子，分别对应两个观点，因此在解题的时候要注意例子的对应。</td></tr></table>





##### 例62：英语二2018年Text3

①The product they're selling is data, and we, the users, convert our lives to data for the benefit of the digital giants. ②Just as some  $ \underline{\text{ants}} $ farm the bugs called aphids for the honeydew they produce when they feed, so Google farms us for the data that our digital lives yield. ③ $ \underline{\text{Ants}} $ keep predatory insects away from where their aphids feed; Gmail keeps the spammers out of our inboxes. ④It doesn't feel like a human or democratic relationship, even if both sides benefit.

①它们（数字巨头）销售的产品是数据，而作为用户的我们将自己的生活转化为数据，为数字巨头的利益服务。②正如有些蚂蚁养殖一种叫作蚜虫的小虫子是为了获取它们进食时分泌的蜜露，谷歌“养殖”我们（向我们提供服务）是为了得到我们数字生活所产生的数据。③蚂蚁让捕食性昆虫远离它们的蚜虫进食的地方；谷歌邮箱将垃圾邮件发送者挡在我们的收件箱外。④这不像是一种人性化或民主的关系，即使双方都（从中）获益。

35 The  $ \underline{\text{ants}} $ analogy is used to illustrate _____.

蚂蚁的类比被用来说明_____。

题干定位 根据题干中的关键词 ants（蚂蚁）定位到段 4。



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[A]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>a typical competition pattern among digital giants数字巨头之间的典型竞争模式</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[B]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>a win-win business model between digital giants数字巨头之间双赢的商业模式</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>[C]</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>the benefits provided for digital giants&#x27; customers为数字巨头的顾客提供的好处</td></tr></table>

【段4】① $ \underline{\text{The product they're selling}} $ is data, and we, the users, convert our lives to data for the benefit of the digital  $ \underline{\text{giants}} $. ②Just as some ants farm the bugs called aphids for the honeydew they produce when they feed, so Google farms us for the data that our digital lives yield. ③Ants keep predatory insects away from where their aphids feed; Gmail keeps the spammers out of our inboxes. ④ $ \underline{\text{It doesn't feel like a human}} $ or democratic relationship, even if both sides benefit.

根据题干中的 ants（蚂蚁）可以定位到段 4 句②~③，这部分是例子的具体内容，要在例子前后找其服务的观点或主旨，因此要看段 4 句①和句④。段 4 句①指出“它们（数字巨头）销售的产品是数据，而作为用户的我们将自己的生活转化为数据，为数字巨头的利益服务”；句④指出“这不像是一种人性化或民主的关系，即使双方都（从中）获益”。其中，句④中的 both sides（双方）指代的就是句①

the relationship between digital giants and their

[D] use

中的 the users（用户）和 the digital giants（数字巨头）。由此知，这两句话都在讲二者之间的关系，并由此可判断以蚂蚁作类比就是为了说明这一关系。D选项 the relationship between digital giants and their users（数字巨头和它们的用户之间的关系）符合这一含义，因此D选项正确。

字巨头和它们的用户之间的关系

A 选项中的 among digital giants（数字巨头之间）、B 选项中的 between digital giants（数字巨头之间）和 C 选项中的 customer（顾客）都只提到了原文中的 both sides（双方）的其中一方，与原文不符，因此排除。

这道题的特别之处在于选项的分析。在解题时，如果发现选项有相同点，那么可以找到相同而比较不同，或者是把选项分类。本题的A、B两个选项范围都是在“数字巨头之间”，C选项针对的是“数字巨头的顾客”，而D选项指的是“数字巨头和它们的用户之间”。厘清四个选项的范围，再结合例子，能够更清晰准确地找到答案

[A] Strain of Stress: No Way Out?

25. Which of the following would be the best title for the text?

[B] Responses to Stress: Gender Difference

[C] Stress Analysis: What Chemicals Say

[D] Gender Inequality: Women Under Stress

① While still catching up to men in some spheres of modern life, women appear to be way ahead in at least one undesirable category. ② "Women are particularly susceptible to developing depression and anxiety disorders in response to stress compared to men," according to Dr. Yehuda, chief psychiatrist at New York's Veteran's Administration Hospital.

① Studies of both animals and humans have shown that sex hormones somehow affects the stress response, causing females under stress to produce more of the trigger chemicals than do males under the same conditions. ② In several of the studies, when stressed-out female rats had their ovaries (the female reproductive organs) removed, their chemical responses became equal to those of the males.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5005d001-ac30-4eeb-b626-bbefdc57a842/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_164_1471_227_1523.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2F537528809f5a9e66bd4bcc38f68477467e0fb3c0f42eec242bc03551a8da565d" alt="Image" width="5%" />

 $ \frac{3}{2} $ ① Adding to a woman's increased dose of stress chemicals, are her increased "opportunities" for stress. ② "It's not necessarily that women don't cope as well. ③ It's just that they have so

much more to cope with," says Dr. Yehuda. ④ "Their capacity for tolerating stress may even be greater than men's," she observes, "It's just that they're dealing with so many more things that they become worn out from it more visibly and sooner."

① Dr. Yehuda notes another difference between the sexes. ② "I think that the kinds of things that women are exposed to tend to be in more of a chronic or repeated nature. ③ Men go to war and are exposed to combat stress. ④ Men are exposed to more acts of random physical violence. ⑤ The kinds of interpersonal violence that women are exposed to tend to be in domestic situations, by, unfortunately, parents or other family members, and they tend not to be one-shot deals. ⑥ The wear-and-tear that comes from these longer relationships can be quite devastating."

例64：英语—2017年Text3

35. Which of the following is the best title for the text?

[A] Brexit, the UK's Gateway to Well-being

[B] Robert F. Kennedy, a Terminator of GDP

[C] High GDP But Inadequate Well-being, a UK Lesson

[D] GDP Figures, a Window on Global Economic Health

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5005d001-ac30-4eeb-b626-bbefdc57a842/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_119_1182_196_1239.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A41Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa4b36f1569ba145627be65a0b23ec90febac61f6c06b452df7c3a7a3d06a3819" alt="Image" width="6%" />

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5005d001-ac30-4eeb-b626-bbefdc57a842/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_119_1182_196_1239.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A41Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa4b36f1569ba145627be65a0b23ec90febac61f6c06b452df7c3a7a3d06a3819" alt="Image" width="6%" />

段1 $ ^{①} $

</div>


</div>


① Robert F. Kennedy once said that a country's GDP measures "everything except that which makes life worthwhile." ② With Britain voting to leave the European Union, and GDP already predicted to slow as a result, it is now a timely moment to assess what he was referring to.

① The question of GDP and its usefulness has annoyed policymakers for over half a century.

② Many argue that it is a flawed concept. ③ It measures things that do not matter and misses things that do. ④ By most recent measures, the UK's GDP has been the envy of the Western world, with record low unemployment and high growth figures. ⑤ If everything was going so well, then why did over 17 million people vote for Brexit, despite the warnings about what it could do to their

country's economic prospects?

① A recent annual study of countries and their ability to convert growth into well-being sheds some light on that question. ② Across the 163 countries measured, the UK is one of the poorest performers in ensuring that economic growth is translated into meaningful improvements for its citizens. ③ Rather than just focusing on GDP, over 40 different sets of criteria from health, education and civil society engagement have been measured to get a more rounded assessment of how countries are performing.

① While all of these countries face their own challenges, there are a number of consistent themes. ② Yes, there has been a budding economic recovery since the 2008 global crash, but in key indicators in areas such as health and education, major economies have continued to decline. ③ Yet this isn't the case with all countries. ④ Some relatively poor European countries have seen huge improvements across measures including civil society, income equality and the environment.

① This is a lesson that rich countries can learn: When GDP is no longer regarded as the sole measure of a country's success, the world looks very different.

① So, what Kennedy was referring to was that while GDP has been the most common method for measuring the economic activity of nations, as a measure, it is no longer enough. ② It does not include important factors such as environmental quality or education outcomes—all things that contribute to a person's sense of well-being.

① The sharp hit to growth predicted around the world and in the UK could lead to a decline in the everyday services we depend on for our well-being and for growth. ② But policymakers who refocus efforts on improving well-being rather than simply worrying about GDP figures could avoid the forecasted doom and may even see progress.

##### 例65：英语二2020年Text2

30. The most suitable title for this text would be ___.

[A] CEOs Are Not Overpaid

[B] CEO Pay: Past and Present

[C] CEO Traits: Not Easy to Define

[D] CEOs' Challenges of Today

① It is true that CEO pay has gone up—top ones may make 300 times the pay of typical workers on average, and since the mid-1970s, CEO pay for large publicly traded American corporations has, by varying estimates, gone up by about 500%. ② The typical CEO of a top

American corporation now makes about $18.9 million a year.

① The best model for understanding the growth of CEO pay is that of limited CEO talent in a world where business opportunities for the top firms are growing rapidly. ② The efforts of America's highest-earning 1% have been one of the more dynamic elements of the global economy. ③ It's not popular to say, but one reason their pay has gone up so much is that CEOs really have upped their game relative to many other workers in the U.S. economy.

① Today's CEO, at least for major American firms, must have many more skills than simply being able to "run the company." ② CEOs must have a good sense of financial markets and maybe even how the company should trade in them. ③ They also need better public relations skills than their predecessors, as the costs of even a minor slipup can be significant. ④ Then there's the fact that large American companies are much more globalized than ever before, with supply chains spread across a larger number of countries. ⑤ To lead in that system requires knowledge that is fairly mind-boggling. ⑥ Plus, virtually all major American companies are becoming tech companies, often with their own research and development. ⑦ And beyond this, major CEOs still have to do all the day-to-day work they have always done.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_105_755_182_813.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F20c40c601935a512ff254a5f784311481413dee5d2a7e5583ace9ab6788bdab2" alt="Image" width="6%" />

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_105_755_182_813.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F20c40c601935a512ff254a5f784311481413dee5d2a7e5583ace9ab6788bdab2" alt="Image" width="6%" />

段4 $ ^{①} $

</div>


</div>


① The common idea that high CEO pay is mainly about ripping people off doesn't explain history very well. ② By most measures, corporate governance has become a lot tighter and more rigorous since the 1970s. ③ Yet it is principally during this period of stronger governance that CEO pay has been high and rising. ④ That suggests it is in the broader corporate interest to recruit top candidates for increasingly tough jobs.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_103_974_182_1032.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd1161e90f11541df18bd71b8f834108fb1834b7fccda533c104fdd94de5b18c9" alt="Image" width="6%" />

段5 $ ^{①} $

① Furthermore, the highest CEO salaries are paid to outside candidates, not to the cozy insider picks, another sign that high CEO pay is not some kind of depredation at the expense of the rest of the company. ② And the stock market reacts positively when companies tie CEO pay to say, stock prices, a sign that those practices build up corporate value not just for the CEO.

##### 例66：英语—2017年Text1

25. Which of the following would be the best title for the text?

[A] Getting Stuck in Security Lines

[B] PreCheck—a Belated Solution

[C] Less Screening for More Safety

[D] Underused PreCheck Lanes

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_102_1452_179_1509.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F109a05cb2326996015c3b2afe3ce80dbc7aaf42ec428fbdcb9268e190a27a3c4" alt="Image" width="6%" />

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_102_1452_179_1509.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F109a05cb2326996015c3b2afe3ce80dbc7aaf42ec428fbdcb9268e190a27a3c4" alt="Image" width="6%" />

段1 $ ^{①} $

</div>


</div>


① First two hours, now three hours—this is how far in advance authorities are recommending people show up to catch a domestic flight, at least at some major U.S. airports with increasingly

massive security lines.

① Americans are willing to tolerate time-consuming security procedures in return for increased safety. ② The crash of EgyptAir Flight 804, which terrorists may have downed over the Mediterranean Sea, provides another tragic reminder of why. ③ But demanding too much of air travelers or providing too little security in return undermines public support for the process. ④ And it should: Wasted time is a drag on Americans' economic and private lives, not to mention infuriating.

① Last year, the Transportation Security Administration (TSA) found in a secret check that undercover investigators were able to sneak weapons—both fake and real—past airport security nearly every time they tried. ② Enhanced security measures since then, combined with a rise in airline travel due to the improving economy and low oil prices, have resulted in long waits at major airports such as Chicago's O'Hare International. ③ It is not yet clear how much more effective airline security has become—but the lines are obvious.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_139_706_216_765.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Fedbb8f6fa402e4befc48ff7e2cfbc28350d2f367566ddf6b932df3223e9afd4a" alt="Image" width="6%" />

段4 $ ^{①} $

</div>


</div>


① Part of the issue is that the government did not anticipate the steep increase in airline travel, so the TSA is now rushing to get new screeners on the line. ② Part of the issue is that airports have only so much room for screening lanes. ③ Another factor may be that more people are trying to overpack their carry-on bags to avoid checked-baggage fees, though the airlines strongly dispute this.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_137_934_215_989.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Faa9bcdf8aec584f52bc6dbc81c3f783520103c83a0c11b01b8f078ca17b6bee7" alt="Image" width="6%" />

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d02398be-d15d-4f7d-bb38-1e09eedae083/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_137_934_215_989.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-22T15%3A15%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Faa9bcdf8aec584f52bc6dbc81c3f783520103c83a0c11b01b8f078ca17b6bee7" alt="Image" width="6%" />

段5 $ ^{①} $
